❯ logout                                                                                                                

⏺ To log out of Claude Code, use the built-in command:

  /logout

  Or from your terminal outside of Claude Code:

  claude logout

✻ Baked for 5s

❯ claude login                                                                                                          

⏺ To log in to Claude Code, run this in your terminal:

  claude login

  Or use the built-in slash command within Claude Code:

  /login

  If you need to run it directly from this session, type:

  ! claude login

  The ! prefix runs shell commands within Claude Code and the output will appear in the conversation.

✻ Worked for 5s

❯ claude login

❯ Claude says I am using API Usage Billing but I just upgraded to the pro plan. How do I switch authentication?         

⏺ claude-code-guide(Claude Code auth switching question)
  ⎿  Done (3 tool uses · 22.6k tokens · 11s)
  (ctrl+o to expand)

⏺ To switch from API billing to your Pro subscription:

  1. Run /login in Claude Code — this opens a browser to authenticate with your Claude.ai account.
  2. Check for a lingering API key — if it still shows API billing after logging in, your ANTHROPIC_API_KEY environment
  variable may be taking precedence. Unset it:
  unset ANTHROPIC_API_KEY
  3. Toggle off custom API key — run /config and make sure "Use custom API key" is turned off.
  4. Verify with /status — it should now show your Pro subscription instead of API Usage Billing.

 Here is Claude's plan:                                                                                                 
╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌
 Kroger Coupon Clipper — Implementation Plan                                                                            
                                                                                                                        
 Context                                                                                                                

 Build a web app (portable to mobile later) where the user enters a shopping list and the app automatically clips
 matching digital coupons to their Kroger account. Project starts greenfield at /Users/daniel/dev/kroger (currently
 empty). Audience is the user + family/friends (~5–20 people).

 Critical constraint discovered up front: the official Kroger Public Developer API supports OAuth2, product search,
 location lookup, identity, and cart writes — but it has no coupon-clipping endpoint. Coupon scrape and clip must be
 done via headless-browser automation logged into kroger.com directly. This is technically against Kroger's TOS; the
 user has accepted this for a small private deployment. The architecture below is a hybrid: official API for everything
  it supports, Playwright for what only the website exposes.

 References from research (working open-source examples):
 - CupOfOwls/kroger-api — clean Python wrapper for the public API
 - Shmakov/kroger-cli, suada-a/kroger-coupon-clipper — Selenium-based clip references; the clip flow is "log into
 kroger.com → /savings → click each unclipped coupon's Clip button"

 Tech Stack

 - Next.js 15 (App Router) + TypeScript — UI + /api/* in one codebase, renders fine inside a Capacitor WebView for
 later mobile packaging
 - Separate Node.js worker running Playwright (Chromium) — can't run on serverless; needs a long-lived container
 - Postgres + Prisma
 - Redis + BullMQ for the clip/scrape job queue
 - Tailwind + shadcn/ui
 - Auth.js v5 (Credentials provider, Argon2id) for app login
 - libsodium for credential encryption

 Architecture

 Four containers in one Docker Compose stack:

 - web — Next.js (UI + API routes). Talks to Postgres via Prisma; enqueues BullMQ jobs.
 - worker — Node + Playwright. Subscribes to coupons.scrape and coupons.clip queues. Headless + stealth in prod.
 - postgres, redis.

 Communication: web → Redis enqueue → worker consumes → worker writes results to Postgres → browser polls /api/jobs/:id
  (or SSE). Clip runs are 30–120s, so always async with a job-status page.

 Database tables (Prisma)

 - User — id, email, password_hash, created_at
 - KrogerOAuth — user_id PK, access_token_enc, refresh_token_enc, scopes, expires_at, location_id
 - KrogerCredential — user_id PK, username, password_enc, password_nonce, last_login_at, last_login_status
 - ShoppingList + ShoppingListItem (raw_text, matched_product_id?, matched_upc?)
 - CouponSnapshot — user_id, fetched_at, payload_json, ttl_until (default TTL 6h)
 - ClipJob — id, user_id, list_id, status, started_at, finished_at, summary_json
 - ClipResult — job_id, coupon_id, coupon_title, item_id?, outcome (clipped|already_clipped|not_found|failed),
 error_text?

 Auth — three independent layers, kept straight

 1. App login — Auth.js v5 Credentials provider, email + password, Argon2id, sessions in Postgres, 30-day rolling JWT
 cookie. No social login; small audience.
 2. Kroger Public API per-user OAuth2 — Authorization Code + PKCE. /api/kroger/connect → Kroger authorize →
 /api/kroger/callback exchanges code; tokens encrypted at rest. Scopes: product.compact cart.basic:write
 profile.compact. Used for product search and adding items to the user's Kroger cart.
 3. kroger.com username/password — collected on /settings/clipper, encrypted immediately, never returned to the client
 after save (UI shows masked + "replace" only). Used only by the worker.

 Credential encryption

 Master-key envelope encryption with libsodium secretbox (XSalsa20-Poly1305). 32-byte master key in MASTER_KEY env var,
  fresh 24-byte nonce per credential, store (ciphertext, nonce). Rotation = re-encrypt-on-read with (old_master,
 new_master).

 Why this and not zero-knowledge derivation or KMS: zero-knowledge would force re-entering the app password on every
 clip run (breaks background/auto-runs); KMS is overkill for 5–20 users. This is the same model pass/Vaultwarden use.

 Coupon-clip flow (end-to-end)

 1. User submits a free-text shopping list.
 2. Web normalizes items, calls Kroger Products API (/products?filter.term=...&filter.locationId=...), stores top match
  (UPC/brand/size) on each ShoppingListItem.
 3. Web enqueues coupons.scrape only if CouponSnapshot.ttl_until is expired/missing. Worker logs into kroger.com,
 scrapes /savings, writes a fresh snapshot.
 4. Web matches coupons → matched products with a scored heuristic (brand exact + name token overlap + category). Shows
  the user the proposed matches before clipping (confirmation step prevents wrong clips).
 5. User confirms → web enqueues coupons.clip with {userId, couponIds[]}. Worker reuses the warm browser context if
 present, otherwise re-logs in. For each coupon: locate card, check state, click Clip if needed, wait for state change,
  record outcome.
 6. Worker writes ClipResult rows + ClipJob.summary_json. Results page shows clipped / already-clipped / not-found /
 failed.

 The worker is structured so a single job can chain scrape → match → clip without a second login.

 Project layout (pnpm workspaces monorepo)

 /Users/daniel/dev/kroger/
   apps/
     web/                  # Next.js
     worker/               # Node + Playwright
   packages/
     shared/               # zod schemas, types, Kroger API client, matching logic, DOM selectors
     db/                   # Prisma schema + client
     crypto/               # libsodium envelope encrypt/decrypt
   infra/
     docker-compose.yml
     Dockerfile.web
     Dockerfile.worker     # mcr.microsoft.com/playwright:v1.49-jammy base
   .env.example
   pnpm-workspace.yaml
   turbo.json

 Hosting

 Single $12/mo DigitalOcean droplet (2 vCPU / 2 GB RAM) running Docker Compose, Caddy reverse proxy with auto-TLS. One
 box hosts web, worker, postgres, redis, caddy. Nightly pg_dump to Backblaze B2.

 Why one box: Playwright Chromium needs ~500 MB steady and a persistent process — Vercel/serverless won't work.
 Splitting web to Vercel + worker to Fly doubles deploy/log surface for no benefit at this scale. Add a residential-IP
 proxy (~$5/mo) only if Kroger blocks the datacenter IP.

 Phased delivery

 - M1 — Skeleton + app auth (week 1): Monorepo, Docker Compose, Postgres, Auth.js signup/login/logout, empty dashboard.
  Verify: sign up, log in, log out.
 - M2 — Kroger OAuth + product search (week 2): Connect-Kroger flow, home-store selection, shopping-list UI,
 server-side product search with images. Verify: enter "milk, eggs, oreos", see three matched products with
 store-specific prices.
 - M3 — Worker + coupon scrape (week 3): Worker container, kroger.com credentials page (encrypted), coupons.scrape job,
  snapshot persistence, "Available coupons" page. Verify: save credentials → scrape → see your real coupons within
 ~30s. Re-run should hit cache.
 - M4 — Match + clip (week 4): Matching algorithm, match-confirmation UI, coupons.clip job, results page. Verify: enter
  a list with one item that has a coupon, one already-clipped, one with no coupon — all three outcomes shown correctly.
  Confirm on kroger.com (mobile) the new ones show as clipped.

  Listed 1 directory (ctrl+o to expand)

⏺ The directory is empty — this is a greenfield project. Let me research the Kroger API to understand what's possible
  before planning.

⏺ Explore(Research Kroger Public API capabilities)
  ⎿  Done (17 tool uses · 25.3k tokens · 4m 13s)
  (ctrl+o to expand)

   the official Kroger API.

  coupon to account" endpoint — it supports product search, store lookup, identity, and cart writes, but coupon clipping
   has to go through a different mechanism. I confirmed this against the developer docs and three open-source projects:
  the only working coupon-clippers (Shmakov/kroger-cli, suada-a/kroger-coupon-clipper) all use headless-browser

  ⎿  Done (1 tool use · 17.8k tokens · 2m 25s)

⏺ Writing the plan to file now.

⏺ Updated plan
  ⎿  /plan to preview
  ⎿  Tool use rejected

⏺ The "week" labels were the planning agent's convention for human part-time effort — they're not how long it'll
  actually take with me coding. Real timing:                                              

  Coding effort per milestone (my work):                                                                                
  - M1 (skeleton + app auth): ~1–2 hours
  - M2 (Kroger OAuth + product search): ~2–3 hours                                                                      
  - M3 (Playwright worker + coupon scrape): ~2–4 hours — Playwright on kroger.com is the most likely place to hit     
  surprises                                                                                                             
  - M4 (match + clip + confirmation UI): ~3–5 hours                                                                     
  - M5 (PWA polish): ~1–2 hours                                                                                         
                                                                                                                        
  Total: ~10–16 hours of focused coding. Could be one long weekend, or a couple of evenings.
                                                                                                                        
  The real schedule depends on three things, not coding speed:                                                          
                                                                                                                        
  1. Kroger Developer registration — you need to register an app at developer.kroger.com to get a client ID/secret      
  before M2 can be tested. ~15 minutes on your side, but it's a hard prerequisite. Sometimes Kroger is slow to approve.
  2. Per-milestone verification — each milestone needs you to log in with your real Kroger account, run a real list, and
   confirm clipped coupons appear correctly. That's the real serialization point.                                       
  3. Kroger pushback — if their bot detection flags the worker on first login, M3 could turn into a "buy a residential
  proxy and try again tomorrow" detour. Can't predict this in advance.                                                  
                                                        
  Two ways I can adjust the plan:                                                                                       
                                                        
  - Speedrun: Collapse M1+M2 into one sitting and M3+M4 into another. Less ceremony, fewer verification checkpoints. Get
   to a working clipper in maybe 2 sessions.            
  - Safety-first: Keep the milestones but add explicit "Kroger gotcha" buffers (2FA discovery, captcha discovery,       
  IP-block discovery) that could each push timing.                                                                      
   
  Want me to update the plan with realistic hour-based estimates, and then pick speedrun vs phased? Or are you ready to 
  start building M1?                                    
                                                                                                                        
✻ Sautéed for 7m 10s

  DigitalOcean or any other payed service. It run on docker loacally.                                                   
                                                                                                                        
⏺ Updating the plan to swap hosting for a fully local Docker setup. Two side effects worth noting and incorporating: (1)
   the IP-block risk gets better since home IP is residential by default, and (2) phone access only works on the same   
  Wi-Fi (or via a tunnel like Tailscale).

 present, otherwise re-logs in. For each coupon: locate card, check state, click Clip if needed, wait for state change,
  record outcome.
 6. Worker writes ClipResult rows + ClipJob.summary_json. Results page shows clipped / already-clipped / not-found /
 failed.

 The worker is structured so a single job can chain scrape → match → clip without a second login.

 Project layout (pnpm workspaces monorepo)

 /Users/daniel/dev/kroger/
   apps/
     web/                  # Next.js
     worker/               # Node + Playwright
   packages/
     shared/               # zod schemas, types, Kroger API client, matching logic, DOM selectors
     db/                   # Prisma schema + client
     crypto/               # libsodium envelope encrypt/decrypt
   infra/
     docker-compose.yml
     Dockerfile.web
     Dockerfile.worker     # mcr.microsoft.com/playwright:v1.49-jammy base
   .env.example
   pnpm-workspace.yaml
   turbo.json

 Hosting (first release: fully local, $0)

 Run everything on the user's Mac via Docker Desktop + Docker Compose. One docker-compose up -d starts web, worker,
 postgres, redis. No reverse proxy, no TLS, no cloud — web is reachable at http://localhost:3000 from the Mac, and at
 http://<mac-lan-ip>:3000 from any device on the same Wi-Fi (so the iPhone can use it in M5).

 - Backups: named Docker volume for Postgres + a local make backup target that writes pg_dump to ~/kroger-backups/ (no
 cloud).
 - OAuth redirect URI registered with Kroger as http://localhost:3000/api/kroger/callback — Kroger allows localhost for
  development apps.
 - Uptime = the Mac being awake. For a "use it before going to the store" workflow this is fine; the worker only runs
 when a clip job is enqueued.
 - Phone access while at the store is out of scope for the first release (would require either a tunnel like
 Tailscale/Cloudflare Tunnel or a real deploy). Plan: clip coupons before leaving the house while on home Wi-Fi.
 Re-evaluate if remote access is needed before adding a hosted deploy later.
 - Why this works: Playwright Chromium just needs a long-running process and ~500 MB of RAM, which Docker Desktop on a
 Mac handles without issue. Running on the user's home IP is actually better for Kroger automation than a datacenter IP
  (see Risks).

 Phased delivery

 - M1 — Skeleton + app auth (week 1): Monorepo, Docker Compose, Postgres, Auth.js signup/login/logout, empty dashboard.
  Verify: sign up, log in, log out.
 - M2 — Kroger OAuth + product search (week 2): Connect-Kroger flow, home-store selection, shopping-list UI,
 server-side product search with images. Verify: enter "milk, eggs, oreos", see three matched products with
 store-specific prices.
 - M3 — Worker + coupon scrape (week 3): Worker container, kroger.com credentials page (encrypted), coupons.scrape job,
  snapshot persistence, "Available coupons" page. Verify: save credentials → scrape → see your real coupons within
 ~30s. Re-run should hit cache.
 - M4 — Match + clip (week 4): Matching algorithm, match-confirmation UI, coupons.clip job, results page. Verify: enter
  a list with one item that has a coupon, one already-clipped, one with no coupon — all three outcomes shown correctly.
  Confirm on kroger.com (mobile) the new ones show as clipped.
 - M5 — Polish + PWA (week 5): Web manifest + service worker for installability, mobile-responsive pass, error states,
 Sentry, rate limits. Verify: on the same Wi-Fi as the Mac, open http://<mac-lan-ip>:3000 in mobile Safari, add to Home
  Screen, run a list end-to-end on the phone. (Note: PWA service workers require HTTPS or localhost; Add-to-Home-Screen
  still works over HTTP on a LAN IP, just without offline capability.)
  The real schedule depends on three things, not coding speed:

  1. Kroger Developer registration — you need to register an app at developer.kroger.com to get a client ID/secret
  before M2 can be tested. ~15 minutes on your side, but it's a hard prerequisite. Sometimes Kroger is slow to approve.
  2. Per-milestone verification — each milestone needs you to log in with your real Kroger account, run a real list, and
   confirm clipped coupons appear correctly. That's the real serialization point.
  3. Kroger pushback — if their bot detection flags the worker on first login, M3 could turn into a "buy a residential
  proxy and try again tomorrow" detour. Can't predict this in advance.

  Two ways I can adjust the plan:

  - Speedrun: Collapse M1+M2 into one sitting and M3+M4 into another. Less ceremony, fewer verification checkpoints. Get
   to a working clipper in maybe 2 sessions.
  - Safety-first: Keep the milestones but add explicit "Kroger gotcha" buffers (2FA discovery, captcha discovery,
  IP-block discovery) that could each push timing.

  Want me to update the plan with realistic hour-based estimates, and then pick speedrun vs phased? Or are you ready to
  start building M1?

   1 # Kroger Coupon Clipper                            
   2
   3 A small-group web app (portable to mobile later) that takes a shopping list
     and auto-clips matching digital coupons to the user's Kroger account. Greenf
     ield as of the last planning session.
   4
   5 ## State of the project
   6
   7 - **Status:** plan written, no code yet. User is reviewing the plan before b
     uilding.
   8 - **Plan file:** `/Users/daniel/.claude/plans/i-want-to-build-drifting-ritch
     ie.md` — read it first for full architecture, milestones, and risks. This CL
     AUDE.md is a quick orientation; the plan is the source of truth.
   9 - **Audience:** the user + ~5–20 family/friends. Not a public/SaaS app.
  10
  11 ## Critical constraint (do not relitigate)
  12
  13 The official Kroger Public Developer API has **no coupon-clipping endpoint**
     . Coupon scrape and coupon clip must go through **Playwright automation on k
     roger.com**. This is against Kroger's TOS; accepted for a small private depl
     oyment. HTTP-only coupon clipping has been ruled out (CSRF prevents it).
  14
  15 The architecture is therefore **hybrid**:
  16 - Kroger Public API (OAuth2 authorization_code + PKCE) for product search, s
     tore lookup, identity, cart writes.
  17 - Playwright worker for coupon list scrape + clip + (optional) viewing alrea
     dy-clipped state.
  18
  19 ## Stack and architecture (decided)
  20
  21 - **Web:** Next.js 15 App Router + TypeScript, Tailwind + shadcn/ui
  22 - **Worker:** separate Node.js + Playwright (Chromium) container — needs a l
     ong-running process, never serverless
  23 - **DB:** Postgres + Prisma
  24 - **Queue:** Redis + BullMQ
  25 - **App auth:** Auth.js v5, Credentials provider, Argon2id, Postgres session
     s
  26 - **Layout:** pnpm workspaces monorepo — `apps/{web,worker}` + `packages/{sh
     ared,db,crypto}`
  27 - **Hosting (first release):** fully local — Docker Compose on the user's Ma
     c, `http://localhost:3000`. No cloud, no paid services. Phone access is via
     LAN IP on the same Wi-Fi.
  28
  29 ## Three auth layers — keep them straight
  30
  31 1. **App login** — Auth.js v5, email + password, our DB.
  32 2. **Kroger Public API per-user OAuth** — authorization_code + PKCE, scopes
     `product.compact cart.basic:write profile.compact`. Tokens encrypted at rest
     . Redirect URI: `http://localhost:3000/api/kroger/callback`.
  33 3. **kroger.com username/password** — collected on `/settings/clipper`, encr
     ypted with libsodium `secretbox` (master key in `MASTER_KEY` env var, fresh
     nonce per credential), used only by the Playwright worker. Never returned to
      the client after save.
  34
  35 These three are independent. A change to one should not touch the others.
  36
  37 ## Reference open-source projects
  38
  39 - `CupOfOwls/kroger-api` — Python wrapper for the Public API; structural ref
     erence
  40 - `Shmakov/kroger-cli` — working coupon-clip via Selenium; reference for the
      kroger.com flow
  41 - `suada-a/kroger-coupon-clipper` — second Selenium reference
  42
  43 The clip flow on kroger.com: log in → `/savings` → click each unclipped coup
     on's "Clip" button → wait for state change. Selectors will be centralized in
      `packages/shared/src/kroger-dom.ts` so a redesign breaks one file.
  44
  45 ## Critical files (to be created)
  46
  47 - `apps/worker/src/clipper.ts` — login + scrape + clip; load-bearing
  48 - `packages/shared/src/kroger-api.ts` — Public API client
  49 - `packages/shared/src/kroger-dom.ts` — kroger.com selectors (single source
     of truth)
  50 - `packages/shared/src/matching.ts` — coupon-to-product matching heuristic
  51 - `packages/db/prisma/schema.prisma` — seven tables (User, KrogerOAuth, Krog
     erCredential, ShoppingList[+Item], CouponSnapshot, ClipJob, ClipResult)
  52 - `packages/crypto/src/envelope.ts` — libsodium envelope encrypt/decrypt
  53 - `apps/web/app/api/kroger/{connect,callback}/route.ts` — Kroger OAuth handl
     ers
  54 - `infra/docker-compose.yml`, `infra/Dockerfile.{web,worker}`
  55
  56 ## User-side prerequisites before M2
  57
  58 - Register an app at developer.kroger.com to get a client_id + client_secret
     . Configure redirect URI as `http://localhost:3000/api/kroger/callback`.
  59 - Pick a "home" Kroger store (zip code or store ID).
  60 - Confirm whether 2FA is enabled on the kroger.com account — if yes, the Pla
     ywright login flow needs a different design.

⏺ It's a brand-new account for just this local app, not your Kroger account. The plan calls for three independent auth
  layers — this is the first one:

  ┌───────────────┬────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┬────────────────────────┐
  │     Layer     │                               What it is                               │    When it shows up    │
  ├───────────────┼────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┼────────────────────────┤
  │ App login     │ Email + password for our local Postgres User table                     │ M1 — what you're       │
  │ (now)         │                                                                        │ signing up for now     │
  ├───────────────┼────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┼────────────────────────┤
  │ Kroger OAuth  │ Authorize the app to call the Kroger Public API on your behalf         │ M2                     │
  ├───────────────┼────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┼────────────────────────┤
  │ Kroger OAuth  │ Authorize the app to call the Kroger Public API on your behalf         │ M2                     │
  │               │ (product search, cart writes)                                          │                        │
  ├───────────────┼────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┼────────────────────────┤
  │ kroger.com    │ Your real kroger.com username/password, encrypted at rest, used only   │ M3                     │
  │ login         │ by the Playwright worker for coupon clipping                           │                        │
  └───────────────┴────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┴────────────────────────┘

  They're separate because (a) the app is designed for me + family/friends, so each user needs their own login
  regardless of what Kroger account they connect, and (b) we never want a Kroger token or password as your only
  credential — if Kroger rotates anything, you can still log into the app and re-link.

  For now, just pick anything — your email and any password ≥ 8 chars. It's local-only, in the Postgres container on
  your Mac.

   take ~10 minutes:

  2. Create a new app. Settings:                                                                                        
    - Type/Environment: Production (the sandbox doesn't have real product data; the public API is rate-limited          
  generously enough that production is fine for personal use)

    - Scopes/Products: request access to product.compact, cart.basic:write, profile.compact

⏺ M2 is in the bag — auth, store-picking, and per-store product matching all working end-to-end.

  Before we start M3, one prerequisite question I should have asked earlier:

  Is 2FA enabled on your kroger.com account (the actual shopping account, not the developer one)? It changes the M3
  design materially:
  - No 2FA: Playwright logs in with stored email + password, persists session cookies for ~14 days, re-logs in when
  they expire. Clean.
  - 2FA on: We can't fully automate login. The cleanest pattern is a one-time "session bootstrap" page where you log
  in to kroger.com inside an embedded Chromium window once; we capture the resulting storageState (cookies +
  localStorage) and reuse it. When it eventually expires you redo the bootstrap.

  Either is workable, just different shapes of code. Let me know which it is and I'll start M3 — or if you want to
  pause again, say the word and I'll write up where we are first.

      60 -- Confirm whether 2FA is enabled on the kroger.com account — if yes, the Playwright login flow needs 
         -a different design.                                                                                  
      69 +## Gotchas (learned the hard way)                                                                    
      70  
      62 -## Phased delivery (summary; details in the plan file)                                               
      71 +- **`pnpm up` is `pnpm update`.** Don't name a script `up` — it gets shadowed silently. Same family: 
         +`install`, `add`, `i`. Our scripts use `stack:*` to avoid collisions.                                
      72 +- **Prisma can't see `.env` from the workspace root** when running migrations from monorepo root. Wor
         +karound: `set -a && source .env && set +a && pnpm db:migrate ...`. Or use `dotenv-cli` if this gets a
         +nnoying.                                                                                             
      73 +- **Don't set `declaration: true` in the base tsconfig.** With pnpm's strict (non-flat) `node_modules
         +` and packages re-exporting types from external modules (next-auth in particular), TS emits `TS2742 "
         +inferred type cannot be named without a reference to..."` errors. Apps don't need declaration emit; w
         +orkspace packages export TS source via `"main": "./src/index.ts"` + Next.js `transpilePackages`.     
      74 +- **pnpm 10 blocks postinstall scripts by default.** The repo's root `package.json` has a `pnpm.onlyB
         +uiltDependencies` allowlist — keep it in sync when adding deps with native bindings or generators (Pr
         +isma, Argon2, Sharp, esbuild, Tailwind oxide).                                                       
      75 +- **OAuth redirect URI must match exactly.** Registered as `http://localhost:3000/api/kroger/callback
         +`. Don't add a trailing slash, don't use `127.0.0.1`.                                                
      76 +- **Source is baked into the Docker image at build time** (no bind mount). Code changes need `pnpm st
         +ack:build`. `.env` changes only need `stack:down && stack:up`. Schema changes need `pnpm db:migrate` 
         +on host **and** `stack:build` (so the container's generated Prisma client matches).                  
      77 +- **Containers in Docker Desktop are grouped by compose project name.** Look for `kroger` in the Cont
         +ainers tab; the four services nest under it.                                                         
      78  
      64 -- **M1** Skeleton + app auth                                                                         
      65 -- **M2** Kroger OAuth + product search                                                               
      66 -- **M3** Worker + coupon scrape (encrypted kroger.com credential storage)                            
      79 +## Phased delivery                                                                                   
      80 +                                                                                                     
      81 +- **M1** Skeleton + app auth — **DONE**                                                              
      82 +- **M2** Kroger OAuth + product search — **DONE**                                                    
      83 +- **M3** Worker + coupon scrape (encrypted kroger.com credential storage) — **NEXT**                 
      84  - **M4** Match + clip + confirmation UI
      85  - **M5** PWA polish + LAN-accessible mobile install
      86  
      70 -Coding effort estimate: ~10–16 focused hours total. The "weekN" labels in the plan are conventional p
         -lanning terms, not actual elapsed time. Real bottlenecks are the user's Kroger developer registration
         -, real-account verification per milestone, and any Kroger bot-detection surprises in M3.             
      87 +## User-side prerequisites for M3                                                                    
      88  
      89 +- **Decide on the kroger.com login pattern based on 2FA status:**                                    
      90 +  - No 2FA: stored email + password, Playwright re-logs as needed.                                   
      91 +  - 2FA on: one-time interactive bootstrap that captures `storageState` (cookies + localStorage) and 
         +reuses it; redo on expiry.                                                                           
      92 +- **Have your kroger.com email + password ready** to enter on the in-app settings page once M3 ships.
         + They go through the same encrypted path as the OAuth tokens.                                        
      93 +                                                                                                     
      94  ## Decisions explicitly ruled out
      95  
      96  - HTTP-only coupon clipping (CSRF blocks it)
     ...
       99  - Cloud hosting for the first release (user wants $0, fully local)
      100  - Public sign-up / SaaS
      101  - Phone access from cellular for the first release (LAN-only)
      102 +- Auth.js DB sessions (Credentials + JWT is enough; no Account/Session/VerificationToken tables need
          +ed)                                                                                                 
      103  
      104  ## Open questions (non-blocking; do not decide silently)
      105  
       83 -- Coupon-to-product match threshold and tuning                                                      
      106 +- 2FA path for M3 (waiting on user)                                                                 
      107 +- Coupon-to-product match threshold and tuning (M4)                                                 
      108  - Multi-store households (one Kroger account, two preferred stores)
      109  - Auto-clip-without-confirm toggle (deferred to post-M5)
      110  - Remote access path (Tailscale vs Cloudflare Tunnel vs real deploy) — deferred until after first re
           lease works
      111  
      112  ## Working principles for this codebase
      113  
       90 -- Selectors for kroger.com live in one file, never inline.                                          
      114 +- Selectors for kroger.com live in one file (`kroger-dom.ts`, coming in M3), never inline.          
      115  - The three auth layers are independent — keep their code, tables, and envs separated.
      116  - The worker is the only thing that ever sees kroger.com credentials in plaintext.
      117  - Match-confirmation UI stays in the loop until we have data to justify auto-clip.
      118  - No paid cloud dependencies until the user explicitly asks for a deploy.
      119 +- Don't reach for `shadcn/ui`, `BullMQ`, `Turbo`, or other "we'll need it eventually" deps until the
          + milestone that requires them.

  Quick heads-up while I work: Kroger runs multiple banners under the same backend (Kroger, King Soopers, Smith's,    
  etc.), and the website domain you sign into for coupons depends on which banner. Your Kroger developer app ID looks 
  like a King Soopers app — I'll default the worker to https://www.kingsoopers.com and make it overridable in .env    
  (KROGER_WEB_DOMAIN). If you actually clip from a different domain (e.g. kroger.com, fredmeyer.com), let me know and 
  I'll change the default.                                                                                            

  The other expectation-setting note: M3 is the milestone with the highest risk of "Kroger redesigned X overnight."   
  The first scrape attempt may fail on selectors and need a round or two of iteration. That's normal for browser
  automation, not a sign anything's broken with the architecture.

⏺ M3 is wired up and running. Worker is listening for scrape jobs, web is up.                                   
                                                                                                                      
  Test flow:                                                   
  1. http://localhost:3000 → log in                                                                                   
  2. Settings → scroll to Coupon clipper credentials → enter your kingsoopers.com email + password → Save credentials
  3. Coupons (in the header) → Scrape coupons now                                                                     
  4. You'll get bounced to /coupons?jobId=... with a polling indicator. The first run does a real Kroger login which  
  can take 20–40 s; subsequent runs reuse the session and should be much faster.                                      
  5. When the job completes, the page refreshes and shows the real coupons.                                           
                                                                                                                      
  Realistic expectation for the first attempt: there's a meaningful chance the scrape fails on the first run because  
  of one of:                                                                                                        
  - Selector drift — the login form or coupon-card selectors I wrote are best-guesses; kingsoopers.com may use        
  different data-testid values now. Failure mode: job completes with error: "scrape_failed" or login times out.
  - Bot detection / captcha — Kroger may show a captcha for an automated browser. Failure mode: job completes with    
  credentials_invalid even though they're correct.                                                                    
  - Different login form layout for King Soopers vs generic Kroger.                                                   
                                                                                                                      
  If it fails, paste me the error from the polling banner and the worker log (pnpm stack:logs and look for [scrape    
  ...] lines), and I'll adjust selectors or the login flow. Multiple iteration rounds are normal.

  Coupons page and tell me what happens.

⏺ That's ERR_HTTP2_PROTOCOL_ERROR before any page loads — classic Akamai (kingsoopers.com's CDN) bot-detection killing
   the TLS/HTTP/2 connection based on browser fingerprint. The headless-shell Chromium that Playwright uses by default
   has a recognizable signature.                               
                                                          
  Trying three fixes together:                
  1. Force HTTP/1.1 (less fingerprinting surface)     
  2. Use the full Chromium channel instead of headless-shell (closer to a real browser)
  3. Update the UA string to current Chrome

⏺ HTTP/2 issue is gone — the warm-up + full Chromium worked. New error: ReferenceError: __name is not defined. This is
   a known tsx/esbuild issue: esbuild injects __name(fn, "name") helpers into compiled code, and when Playwright
  serializes the $$eval callback to run in the browser, those references go with it but the browser has no __name
  defined.

  Fix: inject a small __name polyfill via addInitScript so the browser context has it before our callback runs.

⏺ Update(apps/worker/src/scrape.ts)
  ⎿  Added 8 lines
      58        locale: "en-US",
      59        timezoneId: "America/Denver",
      60      });
      61 +                                                                                                     
      62 +    // Polyfill: tsx/esbuild emits `__name(fn, "x")` calls when transforming                         
      63 +    // local const arrow functions; those references survive into the strings                        
      64 +    // we ship to $$eval, but the browser has no `__name`. Define one.                               
      65 +    await context.addInitScript(                                                                     
      66 +      `if (typeof globalThis.__name === "undefined") { globalThis.__name = (f) => f; }`,             
      67 +    );                                                                                               
      68 +                                                                                                     
      69      const page = await context.newPage();
      70  
      71      const couponsUrl = `${KROGER_WEB_DOMAIN}${KROGER_DOM.coupons.path}`;

      272 +async function dumpDebug(page: Page, userId: string): Promise<void> {                               
      273 +  const dir = "/tmp/scrape-debug";                                                                  
      274 +  await mkdir(dir, { recursive: true });                                                                   
      275 +                                                                                                    
      276 +  const html = await page.content();                                                                       
      277 +  await writeFile(`${dir}/page.html`, html);                                                        
      278 +                                                                                                           
      279 +  await page.screenshot({ path: `${dir}/page.png`, fullPage: true });                               
      280 +                                                                                                    
      281 +  // Count matches for each candidate card selector individually so we can                          
      282 +  // see which (if any) are on the right track.                                                     
      283 +  const counts: Record<string, number> = {};                                                        
      284 +  for (const sel of KROGER_DOM.coupons.cardSelector) {                                              
      285 +    counts[sel] = await page.locator(sel).count();                                                  
      286 +  }                                                                                                 
      287 +                                                                                                    
      288 +  // Also look for a few generic patterns that might be the real cards.                             
      289 +  const probes = [                                                                                  
      290 +    "[data-testid]",                                                                                
      291 +    "article",                                                                                      
      292 +    'div[role="article"]',                                                                          
      293 +    'div[class*="oupon" i]',                                                                        
      294 +    'a[href*="/coupons/"]',                                                                         
      295 +    'a[href*="/savings/"]',                                                                         
      296 +    "img[alt]",                                                                                     
      297 +  ];                                                                                                
      298 +  const probeCounts: Record<string, number> = {};                                                   
      299 +  for (const sel of probes) {                                                                       
      300 +    probeCounts[sel] = await page.locator(sel).count();                                             
      301 +  }                                                                                                 
      302 +                                                                                                    
      303 +  // Sample of unique data-testid values on the page (useful for finding the                        
      304 +  // real coupon-card test id).                                                                     
      305 +  const testIds = await page.$$eval("[data-testid]", (els) => {                                     
      306 +    const set = new Set<string>();                                                                  
      307 +    for (const el of els) {                                                                         
      308 +      const v = el.getAttribute("data-testid");                                                     
      309 +      if (v) set.add(v);                                                                            
      310 +    }                                                                                               
      311 +    return Array.from(set).slice(0, 100);                                                           
      312 +  });                                                                                               
      313 +                                                                                                    
      314 +  await writeFile(                                                                                  
      315 +    `${dir}/probe.json`,                                                                            
      316 +    JSON.stringify(                                                                                 
      317 +      {                                                                                             
      318 +        userId,                                                                                     
      319 +        url: page.url(),                                                                            
      320 +        title: await page.title(),                                                                  
      321 +        candidateCardSelectors: counts,                                                             
      322 +        probeSelectors: probeCounts,                                                                
      323 +        sampleTestIds: testIds,                                                                     
      324 +      },                                                                                            
      325 +      null,                                                                                         
      326 +      2,                                                                                            
      327 +    ),                                                                                              
      328 +  );                                                                                                
      329 +                                                                                                    
      330 +  log(`debug artifacts written to ${dir}/{page.html,page.png,probe.json}`);                         
      331 +}

⏺ Bigger problem than I thought — we're not actually logged in. The screenshot shows a "Sign In" button top-right, and
   the page shows SavingsErrorDisplay ("We're not finding any coupons right now").

  My login-check was wrong: I assumed Kroger redirects to /signin if you're not authenticated, but kingsoopers.com
  just renders a "Sign In" button on the page instead of redirecting. So our if (url.includes("/signin")) check was
  always false, and we silently skipped login. The previous "session reused" runs were scraping a logged-out page that
   has no coupons.

  The fix: detect login state by looking at a specific element on the page, not the URL.

  Searched for 2 patterns (ctrl+o to expand)

      194 +async function isLoggedIn(page: Page): Promise<boolean> {                                           
      195 +  const text = await page                                                                           
      196 +    .locator('[data-testid="WelcomeButtonDesktop"]')                                                
      197 +    .first()                                                                                               
      198 +    .textContent({ timeout: 5_000 })                                                                
      199 +    .catch(() => null);                                                                                    
      200 +  if (text === null) return false;                                                                  
      201 +  return !/sign\s*in|sign\s*up/i.test(text);                                                               
      202 +}

⏺ The smoking gun is ModalityTombstone-animated-background in the HTML — that's the loading skeleton for modality
  (which store/pickup mode you're shopping). It's stuck loading. The XHR that auto-resolves modality from your account
   preferences is being blocked or stalled, which means the coupons-fetch downstream of it never fires. This is
  classic Akamai bot detection blocking specific XHRs while letting the HTML through.                                 
                                                                                   
  Bringing out the bigger hammer: playwright-extra + the stealth plugin. It applies dozens of fingerprint tweaks      
  specifically tuned for Akamai/Cloudflare/Imperva.

⏺ Two things going on, both fixable:                                         
                                                          
  1. The 401 is your Kroger refresh token dying (Kroger rotates them aggressively; ours has gotten stale over the last
   couple days). The path forward is to reconnect — but right now the dead row stays in the DB and the page tries to
  refresh on every render, surfacing the 401. I'll make getValidAccessToken delete the row on 401 so you're
  auto-prompted to reconnect.                          
  2. No address in Home store is just a Settings UX gap — I never added a fetch of the current location's
  name+address. Adding that now.                   
                                                                                                                      
  After both fixes, you'll: see "Connect Kroger account" again → reconnect → search your ZIP (try 80113 for Englewood,
   not 80026) → see addresses next to each result → pick the right store. Then we go back to M3.

         -URI: `http://localhost:3000/api/kroger/callback`. Tables: `KrogerOAuth`. **Implemented.**

         -nly** by the Playwright worker. Never returned to the client after save. Table: `KrogerCredential`. *
         -*Pending M3.**

       79 +## kingsoopers.com / Kroger banner idiosyncrasies (M3)                                              
       80  
       69 -## Gotchas (learned the hard way)                                                                   
       81 +These have all bitten us during M3 implementation. Worth knowing before touching scraper code:      
       82  
       71 -- **`pnpm up` is `pnpm update`.** Don't name a script `up` — it gets shadowed silently. Same family:
          - `install`, `add`, `i`. Our scripts use `stack:*` to avoid collisions.                              
       72 -- **Prisma can't see `.env` from the workspace root** when running migrations from monorepo root. Wo
          -rkaround: `set -a && source .env && set +a && pnpm db:migrate ...`. Or use `dotenv-cli` if this gets
          - annoying.                                                                                          
       73 -- **Don't set `declaration: true` in the base tsconfig.** With pnpm's strict (non-flat) `node_module
          -s` and packages re-exporting types from external modules (next-auth in particular), TS emits `TS2742
          - "inferred type cannot be named without a reference to..."` errors. Apps don't need declaration emit
          -; workspace packages export TS source via `"main": "./src/index.ts"` + Next.js `transpilePackages`. 
       74 -- **pnpm 10 blocks postinstall scripts by default.** The repo's root `package.json` has a `pnpm.only
          -BuiltDependencies` allowlist — keep it in sync when adding deps with native bindings or generators (
          -Prisma, Argon2, Sharp, esbuild, Tailwind oxide).                                                    
       75 -- **OAuth redirect URI must match exactly.** Registered as `http://localhost:3000/api/kroger/callbac
          -k`. Don't add a trailing slash, don't use `127.0.0.1`.                                              
       83 +- **Login is NOT on kingsoopers.com.** kingsoopers.com/signin redirects to `https://login.kroger.com
          +/eciamp.onmicrosoft.com/...` — Microsoft Azure B2C. Login form selectors:                           
       84 +  - Email: `#signInName`                                                                            
       85 +  - Password: `#password`                                                                           
       86 +  - Submit: `button#continue[aria-label="Sign In"]` — note: the HTML contains a Mustache-template sc
          +affold of this button (disabled, `aria-label` is unrendered template syntax) PLUS the real one. Targ
          +et by aria-label, not just by id or `button[type="submit"]`.                                        
       87 +- **Login redirect chain takes 30–50 seconds.** B2C → SelfAsserted → connect-auth → home. `waitForUR
          +L` after submit needs at least a 60 s timeout.                                                      
       88 +- **Login state can't be detected by URL.** kingsoopers.com does NOT redirect logged-out users to /s
          +ignin — it just renders a "Sign In" button on the page. Detect via the `[data-testid="WelcomeButtonD
          +esktop"]` text content (says "Sign In" if logged out, the user's name if logged in).                
       89 +- **Akamai bot detection** is in front of the site. Without correct fingerprint, you get `ERR_HTTP2_
          +PROTOCOL_ERROR` on connection. Mitigations that work:                                               
       90 +  - `chromium.launch({ headless: true, channel: "chromium" })` — full Chromium, NOT headless-shell  
       91 +  - Launch flags: `--disable-http2`, `--disable-blink-features=AutomationControlled`, `--no-sandbox`
          +, `--disable-dev-shm-usage`                                                                         
       92 +  - Realistic UA (Chrome 131+ on macOS); viewport 1280×900; `locale: "en-US"`, `timezoneId: "America
          +/Denver"`                                                                                           
       93 +  - Warm-up homepage visit before navigating to the target page                                     
       94 +- **`playwright-extra` + stealth plugin BACKFIRES.** It breaks kingsoopers.com's bootstrap JavaScrip
          +t, and /signin no longer redirects to Microsoft B2C — page just stays blank. **Don't add it back.** 
          +The plain `playwright-core` config above is the working baseline.                                   
       95 +- **Modality (preferred store + pickup/delivery) is required for the coupons API.** Without it, `htt
          +ps://kingsoopers.com/savings/cl/coupons` SSR-renders `[data-testid="SavingsErrorDisplay"]` ("We're n
          +ot finding any coupons right now"). On a fresh worker session, the modality auto-resolution XHR is s
          +tuck or never resolves — the page renders a `[data-testid="CurrentModalityTombstone"]` placeholder f
          +orever. Need to drive the modality picker manually. The user's account preferred store may differ fr
          +om our app's home store; we want our home store to win.                                             
       96 +- **Coupons are loaded client-side via XHR**, after the static HTML arrives. Use `waitForLoadState("
          +networkidle")` (with a generous timeout, kingsoopers fires background XHRs continuously) plus an `au
          +toScroll` step before scraping cards.                                                               
       97 +- **Selectors are mostly `data-testid`.** Generic class selectors like `div.kds-Card` match scaffold
          +ing (`savinghelpcard`) rather than real coupon cards. The real-coupon-card test ID is **TBD** — only
          + renders once modality is set, which is the current blocker.                                        
       98 +- **Refresh tokens go stale fast.** Kroger rotates / revokes refresh tokens within a few days. `getV
          +alidAccessToken` deletes the OAuth row on 401 from the token endpoint so the user is prompted to rec
          +onnect on the next page load.                                                                       
       99 +- **`/locations/{id}` returns `{data: <single>}`**, not `{data: [...]}` (the search endpoint shape).
          + Schemas are split in `kroger.ts` accordingly.                                                      
      100 +- **The user's locationId format is `<3-digit-banner-prefix><5-digit-store>`** (e.g., King Soopers `
          +62000138` → store #00138). The banner prefix for King Soopers is `620`. Other banners have other pre
          +fixes.                                                                                              
      101 +                                                                                                    
      102 +## Gotchas (general — learned the hard way)                                                         
      103 +                                                                                                    
      104 +- **`pnpm up` is `pnpm update`.** Don't name a script `up` — it gets shadowed silently. Same family:
          + `install`, `add`, `i`. Our scripts use `stack:*`.                                                  
      105 +- **Prisma can't see `.env` from the workspace root** when running migrations from monorepo root. Wo
          +rkaround: `set -a && source .env && set +a && pnpm db:migrate ...`.                                 
      106 +- **Don't set `declaration: true` in the base tsconfig.** With pnpm's strict (non-flat) `node_module
          +s` and packages re-exporting types from external modules (next-auth in particular), TS emits `TS2742
          + "inferred type cannot be named without a reference to..."`. Apps don't need declaration emit; works
          +pace packages export TS source via `"main": "./src/index.ts"` + Next.js `transpilePackages`.        
      107 +- **pnpm 10 blocks postinstall scripts by default.** Root `package.json`'s `pnpm.onlyBuiltDependenci
          +es` allowlist must include any deps with native bindings or generators (`@node-rs/argon2`, `@prisma/
          +client`, `@prisma/engines`, `@tailwindcss/oxide`, `esbuild`, `prisma`, `sharp`).                    
      108 +- **OAuth redirect URI must match exactly.** `http://localhost:3000/api/kroger/callback`. No trailin
          +g slash. Don't use `127.0.0.1`.                                                                     
      109  - **Source is baked into the Docker image at build time** (no bind mount). Code changes need `pnpm s
           tack:build`. `.env` changes only need `stack:down && stack:up`. Schema changes need `pnpm db:migrate
           ` on host **and** `stack:build` (so the container's generated Prisma client matches).
      110 +- **Pin `playwright-core` EXACTLY (no caret) and keep `Dockerfile.worker`'s `mcr.microsoft.com/playw
          +right:v<version>-jammy` tag in lockstep.** Mismatch causes `Executable doesn't exist at /ms-playwrig
          +ht/chromium_headless_shell-XXXX/...` because the image bundles only the matching browser binary.    
      111 +- **Playwright's Docker image ships with stale corepack signing keys.** `corepack prepare pnpm@<rece
          +nt-version>` fails with "Cannot find matching keyid". Workaround in `Dockerfile.worker`: `npm instal
          +l -g pnpm@<version>` instead of corepack.                                                           
      112 +- **tsx/esbuild emits `__name(fn, "name")` helper calls.** When a function is passed to Playwright's
          + `page.$$eval`/`evaluate`, those references survive serialization but the browser has no `__name`. I
          +nject a polyfill via `context.addInitScript('if (typeof globalThis.__name === "undefined") { globalT
          +his.__name = (f) => f; }')` BEFORE running any eval.                                                
      113 +- **BullMQ in Next.js logs a "Critical dependency" warning** because of dynamic requires in `child-p
          +rocessor.js`. Add `bullmq` and `ioredis` to `serverExternalPackages` in `next.config.mjs`.          
      114  - **Containers in Docker Desktop are grouped by compose project name.** Look for `kroger` in the Con
           tainers tab; the four services nest under it.
      115 +- **Debug-dump pattern saved a lot of time.** When a scraper run lands on an unexpected page, the wo
          +rker writes HTML + full-page screenshot + a `probe.json` (with selector match counts and frequent te
          +st-ids) to `/tmp/scrape-debug/<stage>.{html,png}` + `<stage>-probe.json`. Pull with `docker cp` and 
          +read the JSON before guessing selectors. `SCRAPE_DEBUG=1` toggles this.                             
      116

      144  ## Working principles for this codebase
      145  
      114 -- Selectors for kroger.com live in one file (`kroger-dom.ts`, coming in M3), never inline.          
      146 +- Selectors for kroger.com banners live in **one file** (`packages/shared/src/kroger-dom.ts`), never
          + inline.                                                                                            
      147  - The three auth layers are independent — keep their code, tables, and envs separated.
      148  - The worker is the only thing that ever sees kroger.com credentials in plaintext.
      149  - Match-confirmation UI stays in the loop until we have data to justify auto-clip.
      150  - No paid cloud dependencies until the user explicitly asks for a deploy.
      119 -- Don't reach for `shadcn/ui`, `BullMQ`, `Turbo`, or other "we'll need it eventually" deps until the
          - milestone that requires them.

          +s them.

⏺ Two real bugs in my code:                                                                                           
                                                                                                                      
  1. waitForURL returned too early. Login redirected us to /connect-auth, which is the OAuth callback page where      
  MSAL.js still has work to do (exchange code → set session cookies). My predicate just said "leave login.kroger.com" 
  so it returned true on /connect-auth. I navigated away before MSAL finished, losing the session — that's why the
  coupons page shows "Sign In" again.                                                                                 
  2. My modality auto-resolve check was buggy — !document.querySelector('CurrentModalityTombstone') returns true when
  the page hasn't rendered anything yet (no tombstone because nothing's there). Need to also positively check for the 
  vanity name.                                                                                                        
                                                                                                                      
  Fixing both.

      89 -- **Login redirect chain takes 30–50 seconds.** B2C → SelfAsserted → connect-auth → home. `waitForURL
         -` after submit needs at least a 60 s timeout.                                                               
      89 +- **Login redirect chain takes 30–50 seconds.** B2C → SelfAsserted → connect-auth → home. `waitForURL
         +` after submit needs at least a 60 s timeout AND must wait until URL is OFF `/connect-auth` — that's        
         +where MSAL.js exchanges the code and sets session cookies. Navigating away from `/connect-auth` early
         + leaves the session uninitialized, and the next page renders as logged-out even though login form sub       
         +mission succeeded.                                                                                   
      90 +- **Modality auto-resolve check needs both conditions:** no `CurrentModalityTombstone` AND `CurrentMo
         +dality-vanityName` has non-empty text. Just-no-tombstone returns a false positive when the page hasn'
         +t started rendering yet.                                                                             
      91 +- **The user's kroger.com account preferred store and our app's home store can be different.** kingso
         +opers.com auto-resolves to the *account* preferred store on every fresh session (override-via-picker 
         +is required to use a different store).                                                               
      92  - **Login state can't be detected by URL.** kingsoopers.com does NOT redirect logged-out users to /si
          gnin — it just renders a "Sign In" button on the page. Detect via the `[data-testid="WelcomeButtonDes
          ktop"]` text content (says "Sign In" if logged out, the user's name if logged in).
      93  - **Akamai bot detection** is in front of the site. Without correct fingerprint, you get `ERR_HTTP2_P
          ROTOCOL_ERROR` on connection. Mitigations that work:
      94    - `chromium.launch({ headless: true, channel: "chromium" })` — full Chromium, NOT headless-shell
